They don&#39;t just criticize the way they slaughter them, but&amp;nbsp; the fact that they are killing them in the first place. How do you think the Japanese feel about the way they are portrayed in that movie?&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;When it comes to shark fin soup, there are plenty of people who just blame the Chinese for the shark finning that is going on. Again, we are demonizing a culture and it is us (the good guys) vs. them (the bad guys) Aside from the fact that it is not just the Chinese that are to blame, ( watch the video below) it is simply not helpful.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;iframe allowfullscreen=&quot;&quot; frameborder=&quot;0&quot; height=&quot;281&quot; mozallowfullscreen=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;//player.vimeo.com/video/88988649&quot; webkitallowfullscreen=&quot;&quot; width=&quot;500&quot;&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://vimeo.com/88988649&quot;&gt;Guang Zhou Market for Sea Shepherd USA&lt;/a&gt; from &lt;a href=&quot;http://vimeo.com/oceaniclove&quot;&gt;Gary Stokes&lt;/a&gt; on &lt;a href=&quot;https://vimeo.com/&quot;&gt;Vimeo&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;I think the first thing we have to do is realize that a shark is just a fish and a dolphin is just an animal. The issue is not weather we love them or not, but rather is the taking of these animals sustainable, is the killing humane etc.&amp;nbsp; To give you an example, most of you who read this are probably living in the western world and being used to its customs. So when we attack the Japanese for eating dolphins, the Chinese for eating shark fin soup and the Koreans for eating dogs, because it&#39;s just not cool to eat those animals, we don&#39;t consider what other cultures, e.g: India, must think about our custom of eating &quot;holy cows&quot;.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;I know, it hurts to see a shark killed, a dolphin slaughtered or a dog eaten, but if we demonize the ones that are doing it, we won&#39;t really get them to change. It&#39;s just like in politics each side is just blaming and demonizing the other and nothing gets done. &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;It&#39;s easy to get fellow conservationists to agree with us, but how do we get those who don&#39;t agree with us, to see our way? As painful as it might be, we actually have to seek a dialogue with those who don&#39;t see things our way. There are many individuals and organizations that get it and are doing exactly that.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-1ew2R6zFXRw/UyjqVJRoEqI/AAAAAAAAAw8/m3qClNL-nJA/s1600/bull+shark+fiji+1.jpg&quot; imageanchor=&quot;1&quot; style=&quot;clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;&quot;&gt;&lt;img border=&quot;0&quot; height=&quot;268&quot; src=&quot;http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-1ew2R6zFXRw/UyjqVJRoEqI/AAAAAAAAAw8/m3qClNL-nJA/s1600/bull+shark+fiji+1.jpg&quot; width=&quot;320&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;In Fiji, Beqa Adventure divers helped establish the &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.fijisharkdive.com/conservation/shark-reef-marine-reserve&quot;&gt;shark reef marine reserve&lt;/a&gt;, which included involving 3 fishing villages who&#39;s fishermen agreed not to fish in that area in exchange for receiving a fee from all divers, diving in that area. After 10 years of protecting shark reef, a fisherman told &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.blogger.com/profile/06787762757245289307&quot;&gt;Mike Neumann&lt;/a&gt; that before the shark reef marine reserve was established, he could not catch any fish from shore, but now there are plenty of fish there, a spillover effect. This is a great example of conservationist seeking a dialogue with the fishermen and working together to make changes.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;Another example is the &lt;a href=&quot;http://sharkfriendlymarinas.org/&quot;&gt;shark friendly marinas&lt;/a&gt; project. By talking to marinas that are home to many sportfishermen, it got some of those marinas to agree to not allow any caught sharks to be landed there. Again, this project is relying on seeking a dialogue with those who are fishing for sharks and make them aware of the problem associated with shark fishing.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://ultimatesharkchallenge.squarespace.com/storage/shark-research/BobHammerTag.jpg?__SQUARESPACE_CACHEVERSION=1304506107114&quot; imageanchor=&quot;1&quot; style=&quot;clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;&quot;&gt;&lt;img border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://ultimatesharkchallenge.squarespace.com/storage/shark-research/BobHammerTag.jpg?__SQUARESPACE_CACHEVERSION=1304506107114&quot; height=&quot;320&quot; width=&quot;251&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;Yet another example are fishing tournaments. Guy Harvey is someone well known in the fishing industry and a sponsor of many &lt;a href=&quot;http://ultimatesharkchallenge.squarespace.com/&quot;&gt;fishing tournaments.&lt;/a&gt; It&#39;s easy to condemn shark fishing tournaments, and demonize the fishermen participating in it. But here is how I see it. Instead of having a tournament that catches and kills the sharks, they now catch, tag and release the sharks. Is this ideal? Do all the released &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.sharkdiver.com/&quot;&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt; survive? No, of course not. But it is way better than the catch and kill tournaments and it makes the fishermen involved in the conservation efforts. Also Guy Harvey, a fisherman, supports many other &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.guyharvey.com/conservation-partners/&quot;&gt;ocean related conservation efforts&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;And who would have thought that the consumption of shark fin soup in China could decline by 70%? Efforts by various groups and Chinese celebrities have turned the tide and it&#39;s no longer considered fashionable to serve shark fin soup in China. Again, education and working with a culture instead of against it, has shown results. &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;It is perfectly fine to love and care about the sharks! I do! We just have to remember that in order to change things, we should seek a dialogue with those who don&#39;t see things our way and not just condemn and demonize them. If we only accept a world where nobody kills any sharks and we are not willing to compromise, we will never get things to change. We also have to be prepared to be attacked and ridiculed by our fellow conservationists, for working with the &quot;enemy&quot;. Personally, if I can do something that saves just one shark, I don&#39;t care what anyone thinks. If they call me a traitor for supporting a catch and release tournament, so be it. For me it&#39;s not about the praise of my fellow shark lovers, but about saving the sharks.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;OK enough of my rant, I just had to get this off my chest.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;UFICommentBody&quot; data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0&quot;&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=&quot;.5l.1:3:1:$comment606214019465458_70429436:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0:$comment-body.0.$end:0:$0:0&quot;&gt;Cheers,&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span data-ft=&quot;{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}&quot; data-show-faces=&quot;true&quot; data-width=&quot;450&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://www.grindtv.com/&quot;&gt;Grind TV&lt;/a&gt; has a nice article about our breaching &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.sharkdiver.com/&quot;&gt;great white sharks&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv&quot;&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;It&#39;s nice to see that the media has caught on to the fact that &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.sharkdiver.com/&quot;&gt;great white sharks&lt;/a&gt; are not only breaching in South Africa. Thank you &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.facebook.com/pete.thomas.771?fref=ts&quot;&gt;Pete Thomas&lt;/a&gt; for a nice &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.grindtv.com/wildlife/rare-great-white-shark-breach-videotaped-at-guadalupe-island/#x80F3Up4OwA7kyIH.97&quot;&gt;article&lt;/a&gt; and for mentioning Shark Diver.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;copy-paste-block&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;color: blue;&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;color: black;&quot;&gt;Pete Thomas writes:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;color: blue;&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;Gerardo del Villar posted video clip to Facebook and YouTube this past week, and linked to a Spanish-language &lt;a href=&quot;http://gerardodelvillar.blogspot.mx/2016/01/tiburones-blancos-acrobatas-en-aguas.html&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;blog post&lt;/a&gt; about the island’s white sharks, which rarely breach, and for reasons that are unclear.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;copy-paste-block&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;copy-paste-block&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;color: blue;&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;Del Villar suggested that Guadalupe’s  breaching sharks could be trying to establish dominance in the presence  of other sharks, or to remove parasites.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;copy-paste-block&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;color: blue;&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;color: blue;&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;However, &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.sharkdiver.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Shark Diver’s Martin Graf&lt;/a&gt;,  whose company pioneered shark diving at Guadalupe Island, said that  often it’s the smaller sharks that breach. The larger sharks are the  dominant predators.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;color: blue;&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;color: blue;&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;Said Graf: “There’s no rhyme or reason to it. Usually they breach  without any chum or hang-baits in the water. Early morning and dusk seem  to be their preferred times, but it can happen anytime.”&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;iframe allowfullscreen=&quot;&quot; frameborder=&quot;0&quot; height=&quot;315&quot; src=&quot;https://www.youtube.com/embed/E_6RpK7W2vU&quot; width=&quot;560&quot;&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Read the entire article at &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.grindtv.com/wildlife/rare-great-white-shark-breach-videotaped-at-guadalupe-island/#hofozHm4i3bbfwm6.99&quot;&gt;http://www.grindtv.com/wildlife/rare-great-white-shark-breach-videotaped-at-guadalupe-island/#hofozHm4i3bbfwm6.99&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You can join us and dive with these amazing sharks. We only have a few  spaces left for this season, but are already booking for 2017&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Call us at 619.887.4275 or email staff@sharkdiver.com for more info.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let&#39;s go &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.sharkdiver.com/&quot;&gt;shark diving&lt;/a&gt;!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.sahrkdiver.com/&quot;&gt;Shark Diver &lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://www.sharkdiver.com/&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. So here you see first hand what can happen, when you don&#39;t respect the &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.sharkdiver.com/&quot;&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt;. They are not mindless killers, but neither are they pets that just want to be hugged.
